href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://airberlin.com">airberlin<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Air Berlin PLC &amp; Co. Luftverkehrs KG</b> (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">FWB</a>:&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.boerse-frankfurt.de/global-search/AB1">AB1</a>), branded as <b>airberlin</b> or <b>airberlin.com</b> was a major <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a>. At its peak, it was Germany\'s second-largest airline, as well as <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_airlines_in_Europe" title="List of largest airlines in Europe">Europe\'s tenth-largest airline</a> in terms of passengers carried.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It was headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and had hubs at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin Tegel Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport</a>. It was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">oneworld</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>.\n</p><p>The airline was founded in 1978 by Lelco, an American company. Following German reunification, Air Berlin was sold and became a German company in 1991. It joined the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> alliance in 2012. After years of losses, Air Berlin filed for <a href="/wiki/Insolvency" title="Insolvency">insolvency</a> on 15 August 2017<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and ceased operations on 27 October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" class="thumbcaption">After the merger with LTU in 2007 the new basic LTU scheme was adopted,...</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg/220px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg/330px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg/440px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A319_D-ABGF_DUS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="682" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">... and was used in an interim scheme until the introduction of the new logo,...</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg/220px-AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg/330px-AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg/440px-AirBerlin_B737-800_D-ABBF_MUC_2008-08-13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">... to become this bright red color scheme as featured on this <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a>, which was the airline\'s last livery.</div></div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png/150px-Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png/225px-Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png/300px-Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png 2x" data-file-width="1294" data-file-height="1272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_Air_Berlin_USA_1978.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Original Air Berlin USA logo</div></div></div>\n<p>Originally registered as <b>Air Berlin USA</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the company was founded in 1978 as a wholly owned subsidiary of Lelco, an American agricultural enterprise headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> to operate <a href="/wiki/Air_charter" title="Air charter">charter flights</a> on behalf of German tour operators from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin Tegel Airport</a>, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> holiday resorts.<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg91_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg91-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The co-founders of Air Berlin USA were:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Kim Lundgren, a former Berlin-based <a href="/wiki/Flight_engineer" title="Flight engineer">flight engineer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a>;</li>\n<li>John MacDonald, a former station manager of United States supplemental<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> and charter airline <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Airways" title="Saturn Airways">Saturn Airways</a> at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tempelhof_Airport" title="Berlin Tempelhof Airport">Berlin Tempelhof Airport</a> in the 1960s and subsequent general manager Europe and <a href="/wiki/Vice_president" title="Vice president">vice president</a> at the Berlin Tegel Airport base of the former United States supplemental carrier and charter airline <a href="/wiki/Modern_Air_Transport" title="Modern Air Transport">Modern Air</a> from 1968 until 1974;</li>\n<li>Mort Beyer, Modern Air\'s <a href="/wiki/Executive_vice_president" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive vice president">executive vice president</a> from 1967 until 1971 as well as the airline\'s <a href="/wiki/President_(corporate_title)" title="President (corporate title)">president</a> and vice president of the National Air Carrier Association<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup> in 1971 and founder of United States aviation consultancy Avmark.<sup id="cite_ref-DT_ABStartUp_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT_ABStartUp-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Lelco was the agriculture business of Kim Lundgren\'s family in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-DT_ABStartUp_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT_ABStartUp-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a United States airline, Air Berlin was able to access the <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> airline market. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Berlin\'s special political status meant that the <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin_Air_Corridor" title="West Berlin Air Corridor">air corridors</a> into and out of Tegel Airport could only be used by airlines registered in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> or the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The airline\'s headquarters were initially at Tegel Airport. Leonard Lundgren was the first chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the company was issued an <a href="/wiki/Air_Operator%27s_Certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Operator&#39;s Certificate">airline licence</a> and acquired two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a> jet airliners previously owned by <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">Trans World Airlines</a>, Air Berlin USA commenced revenue services on 28 April 1979 with a flight from Berlin-Tegel to <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fg79_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg79-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Plans were made to start long-haul flights on West Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>-<a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> routes,<sup id="cite_ref-fg79_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg79-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timetable81_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timetable81-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Air_Florida" title="Air Florida">Air Florida</a> (an agreement to that effect had been signed in February 1979).<sup id="cite_ref-fg81_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg81-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1980, two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_City_Jet" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing City Jet">Boeing 737-200</a> were leased from Air Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1981, Air Berlin USA continued its weekly scheduled Boeing 707 service on the Berlin <a href="/wiki/Tegel_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Tegel Airport">Tegel Airport</a> - Brussels - <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a> route;<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> however, by 1982, the 707s had been phased out, and during most of the 1980s, Air Berlin USA operated only a single 737-200<sup id="cite_ref-fg84_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg84-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> or (from 1986) a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">737-300</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg89_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg89-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 1990 and 1991, two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">Boeing 737-400s</a> were also placed into service.<sup id="cite_ref-fg91_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg91-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg90_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg90-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1990.E2.80.932000:_New_investors_and_expansion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990\xe2\x80\x932000:_New_investors_and_expansion">1990\xe2\x80\x932000: New investors and expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1990\xe2\x80\x932000: New investors and expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> led to significant changes to the European aviation market, and in particular in Berlin: German airlines now gained access to the city. In 1991, Air Berlin (which had 90 employees at the time)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> was restructured as <b>Air Berlin <a href="/wiki/Gesellschaft_mit_beschr%C3%A4nkter_Haftung" title="Gesellschaft mit beschr\xc3\xa4nkter Haftung">GmbH</a> &amp; Co. Luftverkehrs <a href="/wiki/Kommanditgesellschaft" title="Kommanditgesellschaft">KG</a></b>, a German-registered company, with several German investors joining Kim Lundgren, the original founder, thereby bringing the ownership in line with German foreign-control requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-1992_737_order_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1992_737_order-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joachim_Hunold&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joachim Hunold (page does not exist)">Joachim Hunold</a> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joachim_Hunold" class="extiw" title="de:Joachim Hunold">de</a>), a former sales and marketing director with <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU International</a>, now led the company.\n</p><p>Following an order for ten <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800</a>, Air Berlin grew and by 1999, the fleet grew to twelve aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-fg99_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg99-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, Air Berlin and <a href="/wiki/Hapag-Lloyd_Flug" title="Hapag-Lloyd Flug">Hapag-Lloyd Flug</a> became the first airlines in the world to have their Boeing 737-800s fitted with <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">blended winglets</a>, wingtip devices that are intended to improve <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficiency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-winglets_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winglets-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Air Berlin introduced scheduled flights (which could be booked directly with the airline rather than via a tour operator) in 1997, initially linking a number of secondary German airports to Mallorca.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> By 2002, 35 percent of Air Berlin\'s tickets were sold directly.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_(2)_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_(2)-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In the same year, the airline expanded beyond holiday destinations as low-fare flights marketed as "City Shuttle" to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> started.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_(2)_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_(2)-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Besides Berlin-Tegel, these routes were opened at six German airports (<a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Airport" title="Dortmund Airport">Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster_Osnabr%C3%BCck_International_Airport" title="M\xc3\xbcnster Osnabr\xc3\xbcck International Airport">M\xc3\xbcnster/Osnabr\xc3\xbcck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Airport" title="Nuremberg Airport">Nuremberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paderborn_Lippstadt_Airport" title="Paderborn Lippstadt Airport">Paderborn/Lippstadt</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_(1)_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_(1)-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> that until then had not been served by one of the rising European low-cost carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_(2)_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_(2)-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In what later became a hallmark for Air Berlin as a "semi-low cost carrier", the airline offered complimentary meals and seat reservations,<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_(1)_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_(1)-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> in contrast to its competitors <a href="/wiki/Buzz_(airline)" title="Buzz (airline)">Buzz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hapag-Lloyd_Express" title="Hapag-Lloyd Express">Hapag-Lloyd Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Express" title="Virgin Express">Virgin Express</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932006:_Becoming_Germany.E2.80.99s_second-largest_airline"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000\xe2\x80\x932006:_Becoming_Germany\xe2\x80\x99s_second-largest_airline">2000\xe2\x80\x932006: Becoming Germany\xe2\x80\x99s second-largest airline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2000\xe2\x80\x932006: Becoming Germany\xe2\x80\x99s second-largest airline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In November 2001, the delivery flight of a Boeing 737-800 fitted with winglets set a record: the aircraft with the registration code D-ABBC flew 8,345 kilometres non-stop from Seattle (<a href="/wiki/Boeing_Field" title="Boeing Field">Boeing Field</a>), USA to Berlin (TXL), Germany in 9 hours, 10 minutes.\n</p><p>In January 2004, Air Berlin announced it would cooperate with <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>, a Vienna-based airline.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> As part of the deal, Air Berlin took a 24% stake in Niki.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png/220px-Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="61" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png/330px-Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png/440px-Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="207" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old Air Berlin logo used from 1986 until 2008.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2005, Air Berlin signed a partnership agreement with <a href="/wiki/Germania_(airline)" title="Germania (airline)">Germania</a>. As part of the deal, Air Berlin leased some of Germania\'s aircraft and crew, and Germania became almost exclusively a charter airline. Plans were made for Germania to be associated with Air Berlin under a management contract. However, the contract was not signed. At the beginning of March 2008, Germania\'s joint owners could not reach agreement on the takeover by Air Berlin, so Germania remained an independent airline. A joint Air Berlin/Germania subsidiary dubbed <i>Air Z\xc3\xbcrich</i> and planned to be based at <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> was proposed in 2005, but did not materialize.\n</p><p>In 2005 the Group reorganised its corporate structure. It established Air Berlin plc (registered in England) into which it reversed Air Berlin GmbH &amp; Co. Luftverkehrs KG and subsidiaries.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> It was suggested that the reason for the group to establish a UK-based PLC instead of a German-based AG was to avoid the need to have a supervisory board and employee representation as required by the German law of <i>Mitbestimmung</i> or <a href="/wiki/Co-determination" title="Co-determination">co-determination</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, Air Berlin <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">went public</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a>. Originally scheduled for 5 May 2006, the IPO was postponed to 11 May 2006. The company said the delay was due to rises in fuel costs and other market pressures limiting investor demand. It reduced the initial share-price range from 15.0\xe2\x80\x9317.5 <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a> to 11.5\xe2\x80\x9314.5 euros. The stock opened at \xe2\x82\xac12.0, selling a total of 42.5 million shares. Of these, 19.6 million were new shares increasing capital in the company, and the remainder to repay loans extended by the original shareholders and invested in the company earlier in 2006. After the IPO, the company claimed to have over 400 million euros in cash to fund further expansion, including aircraft purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2006, Air Berlin acquired German domestic airline <a href="/wiki/DBA_(airline)" title="DBA (airline)">dba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dba_takeover_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dba_takeover-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Flight operations at dba were continued as a fully owned subsidiary of Air Berlin until 14 November 2008, when the dba brand was discontinued due to staff strikes (dba staff were subsequently offered positions with Air Berlin).\n</p><p>On 28 November 2006, Air Berlin ordered 60 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800</a> aircraft,<sup id="cite_ref-boeing_order_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boeing_order-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and 15 smaller <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-700</a> aircraft. The value of the 75 aircraft was 5.1 billion <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">dollars</a> (based on list prices at the time.) Delivery of the aircraft started in 2007. All of these aircraft were equipped with blended <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">winglets</a>, to improve fuel efficiency.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932012:_Takeovers.2C_expansion_and_new_alliances"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007\xe2\x80\x932012:_Takeovers,_expansion_and_new_alliances">2007\xe2\x80\x932012: Takeovers, expansion and new alliances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2007\xe2\x80\x932012: Takeovers, expansion and new alliances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-76Q,_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg/220px-Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg/330px-Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg/440px-Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="718" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-76Q,_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2005, one of Air Berlin\'s <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700s</a> featured a special livery promoting Boeing\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Dreamliner</a></i> program.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg/220px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg/330px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg/440px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Following the takeover of <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU</a> in 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-200">Airbus A330-200</a> <i>(pictured)</i> became part of Air Berlin\'s fleet. This long-haul aircraft enabled the airline to fly to intercontinental destinations like <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> (as in this case, depicting an approach to <a href="/wiki/Suvarnabhumi_Airport" title="Suvarnabhumi Airport">Suvarnabhumi Airport</a> in 2008).</div></div></div>\n<p>In March 2007, Air Berlin took over German leisure airline <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU</a>, gaining access to the long-haul market and becoming the fourth-largest airline group in Europe in terms of passenger traffic. This deal led to the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> aircraft into Air Berlin\'s fleet. On 1 May 2009, the LTU brand was discontinued.\n</p><p>On 7 July 2007, Air Berlin announced an order for 25 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787-8 Dreamliner</a> long-haul aircraft, with further options and purchase rights.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Three additional aircraft of this type were to be leased from <a href="/wiki/International_Lease_Finance_Corporation" title="International Lease Finance Corporation">ILFC</a>.\n</p><p>On 21 August 2007, Air Berlin acquired a 49 percent shareholding in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Swiss</a> charter airline <a href="/wiki/Belair_(airline)" title="Belair (airline)">Belair</a>, the remainder being owned by tour operator Hotelplan.<sup id="cite_ref-DK_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DK-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Following the deal, Belair\'s long-haul business was terminated, and the fleet was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320 family</a> aircraft operating scheduled flights on behalf of Air Berlin as well as charter flights for Hotelplan.\n</p><p>On 20 September 2007, Air Berlin announced it intended to buy its competitor <a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" class="mw-redirect" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor</a> in a deal that envisaged Condor\'s owner, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group" title="Thomas Cook Group">Thomas Cook Group</a>, taking a 30% stake in Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-condor_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-condor-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/2000s_energy_crisis" title="2000s energy crisis">rapidly increasing price of jet fuel</a> and other considerations led to the abandonment of the deal in July 2008.\n</p><p>In January 2008 Air Berlin introduced a new logo and corporate design. The logo is a white oval shape on a red background (suggesting an aircraft window) where the letter "a" is a white circle and two white stylised wings. The text "Air Berlin" was in lower case and written as one word. Sometimes the slogan "Your Airline" was featured as part of the logo.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2008, CEO Joachim Hunold offended <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan language</a> speakers, when he claimed<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> in an article included in Air Berlin\'s <a href="/wiki/In-flight_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="In-flight magazine">in-flight magazine</a> that the government of the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> was trying to impose the use of <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> on Air Berlin flights from and to <a href="/wiki/Majorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>. He claimed that Air Berlin was an international airline and was not obliged to use Catalan. Hunold went on to criticise the language policy in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> and the Balearic Islands, claiming that at the time many children could not speak any <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The Balearic Islands\' President, <a href="/wiki/Francesc_Antich" title="Francesc Antich">Francesc Antich</a>, explained that his government had simply sent a letter to encourage airlines operating in the Balearic Islands to include Catalan among the languages used for onboard announcements.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 June of the same year, Air Berlin announced that it would reduce its long-haul services by 13 percent and its domestic services by 10 percent to increase profitability.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2008, Air Berlin confirmed merger talks with competitor <a href="/wiki/TUI_fly_Deutschland" title="TUI fly Deutschland">TUIfly</a>, but added it was speaking with all parties. Air Berlin had, until 2007, been flying many code-share TUI flights. At the end of March 2009, Air Berlin PLC and TUI Travel PLC signed a deal by which their German flight businesses were to operate a long-term strategic alliance. Originally, each company was to take a 19.9% stake in the other and the German cartel authorities were petitioned for approval. After the Bundeskartellamt expressed concerns, the cross-ownership plan was not implemented. Instead, TUI Travel PLC purchased a 9.9% stake in Air Berlin PLC using a capital increase at a subsidiary to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the end of March 2009, a strategic partnership agreement with <a href="/wiki/TUI_Travel" title="TUI Travel">TUI Travel</a> was signed, with Air Berlin and its competitor <a href="/wiki/TUIfly" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly">TUIfly</a> purchasing 19.9 percent of the other\'s shares.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Following the deal, Air Berlin took over all German domestic TUIfly routes, as well as those to <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. Also, all of Tuifly\'s <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-700</a> aircraft were added to Air Berlin\'s fleet. TUIfly was to abandon all scheduled flights and rely exclusively on the charter business.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2009, ESAS Holding A.S., a Turkish company, bought approximately 15 per cent of the voting shares in Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in 2009, Air Berlin added Hartmut Mehdorn to the board of directors after his retirement at <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable floatleft">\n<caption>Air Berlin Group\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Company\n</th>\n<th>Interest\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>airberlin technik GmbH</td>\n<td align="right">100&#160;%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>airberlin Holidays GmbH</td>\n<td align="right"><span style="visibility:hidden;color:transparent;">0</span>49&#160;%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Belair_(airline)" title="Belair (airline)">Belair</a></td>\n<td align="right">100&#160;%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a></td>\n<td align="right">100&#160;%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In April 2010 Air Berlin expanded its codeshare arrangements with Russia\'s <a href="/wiki/S7_Airlines" title="S7 Airlines">S7 Airlines</a>. Air Berlin and S7 Airlines had cooperated since October 2008. New services included codeshare flights via Moscow to <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perm,_Russia" title="Perm, Russia">Perm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rostov" title="Rostov">Rostov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2010, Air Berlin announced an increase in its shareholding in the <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> airline <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>. Air Berlin indirectly acquired 25.9% of the shares in Niki from Privatstiftung Lauda (private Lauda foundation) and in doing so increased its shareholding in Niki from 24% to 49.9%. In connection with the increase of its shareholding, Air Berlin was to grant the private Lauda foundation a 40.5 million-euro loan. The private foundation had the options to repay the loan in three years with cash or through the transfer of the remaining 50.1% of Niki\'s shares.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D-ABMC_(8629266400)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4249" data-file-height="2833" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D-ABMC_(8629266400)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>After becoming a member of <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a>, several Air Berlin aircraft displayed the alliance\'s logo, as seen on this <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a> on <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> at <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> in 2010, featuring a livery variant using the "Air Berlin" titles on the tail prior to the introduction of the last logo</div></div></div>\n<p>In July 2010, it was also announced that Air Berlin would join <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a>, the global <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In preparation for joining the alliance, Air Berlin made codeshare agreements with <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> starting with the 2010/2011 winter schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Air Berlin founded Follow Me Entertainment GmbH in September 2010 as a joint venture with kick-media ag. This joint-venture company markets image and sound media, books, games as well as events, concerts, tournaments and sponsoring.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 April 2011 Air Berlin completed the integration of LTU. All Air Berlin Group technical services were consolidated in a new company called airberlin technik GmbH.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> It also added new routes, more frequent flights and additional long-haul flights from D\xc3\xbcsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 June 2011, Air Berlin and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> reached a codeshare agreement covering some flights within Europe, starting from 5 July 2011. The agreement applied to flights to over 40 European destinations served by the two airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>CEO Joachim Hunold resigned from his position on 1 September 2011 and was succeeded by the former CEO of Deutsche Bahn AG, Hartmut Mehdorn, who led the company on an interim basis until January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2011 Air Berlin and <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a> (Turkey\'s largest private airline) launched <i>Air Berlin Turkey</i>, aiming at the charter market between Germany and Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a> is 16.5% owned by ESAS Holding AS.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The new airline was absorbed into Pegasus Airlines on 31 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the third quarter of 2011, the turnover of the company amounted to 1.4 billion euros, an increase of 11%. However, operating profit decreased by almost to 50%, around 97 million euros. As a result, a new bond to raise additional capital was issued.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2011 Air Berlin took over the remaining 50.1% stake in NIKI as repayment of a loan and became its sole owner. The brand name was retained and Niki Lauda was given a position on the board of Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Air Berlin announced on 19 December 2011 that the Abu Dhabi airline Etihad Airways had increased its share of Air Berlin from 2.99% to 29.1%, for a sum of 73 million euros, making Etihad the company\'s largest shareholder.<sup id="cite_ref-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The deal supplied more cash to Air Berlin, and provided Etihad access to Air Berlin\'s European network.<sup id="cite_ref-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932015:_Restructuring_amid_continuing_losses"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012\xe2\x80\x932015:_Restructuring_amid_continuing_losses">2012\xe2\x80\x932015: Restructuring amid continuing losses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012\xe2\x80\x932015: Restructuring amid continuing losses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg/220px-Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg/330px-Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg/440px-Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air Berlin aircraft at Terminal C of <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin Tegel Airport</a> in September 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>The cooperation of the frequent-flyer programs topbonus and Etihad Guest was announced in March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In June 2012, the collaboration concluded with the bonus programs airberlin business points and Etihad Airways Business Connect for SMBs.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 March 2012, the entry into oneworld was officially completed.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The Oneworld network offered over 800 destinations in 150 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the airline introduced the Platinum status for its frequent-flyer program topbonus.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2012 Air Berlin presented its new fare structure "Your Fare" including "Just Fly", "Fly Classic" and "FlyFlex" for flights from 1 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May 2012 Air Berlin opened its triweekly non-stop flight from Berlin to Los Angeles in the summer schedule, a destination which until then had only been served from D\xc3\xbcsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 December 2012 Air Berlin announced that <i>topbonus</i>, its frequent flyer program, would be sold to Etihad Airways; only a 30-percent minority share would be retained.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Air Berlin also announced the expansion of the existing codeshare agreement with Etihad Airways on 20 December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2013, the first Airbus A330-200 was introduced with a new business class which enables a fully flat position for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-business_class_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business_class-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 January 2013 Air Berlin appointed Austrian Wolfgang Prock-Schauer, former Chief Strategy and Planning Officer, as the company\'s CEO, replacing Hartmut Mehdorn.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Air Berlin started flights between Berlin and Chicago on 23 March 2013. It cancelled the seasonal non-stop flights to Las Vegas, San Francisco and Vancouver.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2013 Air Berlin announced the closure of its seasonal hub for leisure destinations at <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Airport" title="Nuremberg Airport">Nuremberg Airport</a>. Only ten year-round direct routes remained.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 September 2014, Air Berlin cancelled the remaining 15 orders for their <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787">Boeing 787s</a> as well as 18 remaining orders for <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800s</a> as part of their restructuring programme.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a> denied Air Berlin authorization to operate 34 routes as a codeshare with co-owner Etihad from the 2014/2015 winter schedule as they would contravene the bilateral traffic rights between Germany and the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\nAlso in October 2014, Air Berlin announced the termination of flights to <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a> from both <a href="/wiki/Bremen_Airport" title="Bremen Airport">Bremen Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Airport" title="Dortmund Airport">Dortmund Airport</a>, therefore withdrawing entirely from these two German airports.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Air Berlin announced a net loss for 2014 of \xe2\x82\xac376m (\xe2\x82\xac316m loss in 2013). The airline\'s revenues in 2014 stagnated at \xe2\x82\xac4.16 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_report_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_report-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2015, Air Berlin phased out the last <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700s</a> owned by the company. The remaining aircraft of this type would operate on a wet lease basis from <a href="/wiki/TUIfly" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly">TUIfly</a> until 2019. All <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800s</a> were to be phased out by 2016 as Air Berlin plans to focus their short- and medium-haul fleet on the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320 family</a> to cut costs.<sup id="cite_ref-aero.de-737_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aero.de-737-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2015, Air Berlin announced the closure of its <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">Palma de Mallorca Airport</a> hub by ceasing all of the hub\'s seven Spanish domestic routes by 3 April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PMIshutdown_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMIshutdown-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Some days earlier, the airline announced plans to add flights from D\xc3\xbcsseldorf to Boston, Dallas/Fort Worth, San Francisco and Havana by spring 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> However, the planned route to Dallas/Fort Worth was cancelled a few weeks later due to low demand.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 December 2015, the administrative court in <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig" title="Braunschweig">Braunschweig</a> ruled in favour of the German civil aviation authority (the <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a>) and against Air Berlin regarding some of their codeshare operations with <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>. The shared sale and advertising of 31 out of 83 routes which were marketed by both were declared illegal and ordered stopped by 15 January 2016 as they were not covered by the bilateral air-traffic agreement between Germany and the UAE. The Luftfahrt-Bundesamt had allowed these flights until a definite legal ruling was made.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.932017:_Restructuring_efforts"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016\xe2\x80\x932017:_Restructuring_efforts">2016\xe2\x80\x932017: Restructuring efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2016\xe2\x80\x932017: Restructuring efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In April 2016, Air Berlin announced a record loss of \xe2\x82\xac446 million for 2015; the airline\'s revenues had decreased to \xe2\x82\xac4.08 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_report_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_report-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Amongst the reasons considered for Air Berlin\'s poor performance were: crippling debt of over \xe2\x82\xac800m; unclear and rapid strategy changes on routes and advertising; several <a href="/wiki/CEO" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO">CEOs</a> over recent years; a five-year-plus delay to the new hub <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin Brandenburg Airport</a>; failed negotiations to profit from lower fuel prices and the overall harsh competition in the airline industry.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelmay_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelmay-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, Air Berlin confirmed that it no longer owned any of the aircraft it operates, having sold and leased back the last of the aircraft it had previously owned.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> A few weeks later it was reported that Air Berlin and Etihad Airways were in talks with <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> regarding the latter\'s acquisition of some of Air Berlin\'s routes outside of the Berlin and D\xc3\xbcsseldorf hubs as well as some staff and aircraft leases.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, Air Berlin announced the increase of flights to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> from 55 to 78 nonstops per week for 2017. Besides some frequency increases, Los Angeles and San Francisco were to be served from Berlin as well as by the then existing D\xc3\xbcsseldorf routes. And a new D\xc3\xbcsseldorf-<a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a> route was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A few days later, the airline announced the introduction of a business class on its short- and medium-haul flights.<sup id="cite_ref-newbusinessclass_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newbusinessclass-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2016, Air Berlin announced <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Pichler" title="Stefan Pichler">Stefan Pichler</a>\'s departure after serving two years as CEO and replacement by former head of <a href="/wiki/Germanwings" title="Germanwings">Germanwings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Winkelmann" title="Thomas Winkelmann">Thomas Winkelmann</a> on 1 February.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="The_.22new_Air_Berlin.22_project"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_&quot;new_Air_Berlin&quot;_project">The "new Air Berlin" project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The &quot;new Air Berlin&quot; project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 28 September 2016, Air Berlin announced <i>The new airberlin</i>, a restructuring project including the reduction of its destinations from around 140 to 70, the focus on the Berlin and D\xc3\xbcsseldorf hubs and on the smaller bases in Stuttgart and Munich, the closure of six other bases, the targeting of business travellers, focus on domestic German flights and on flights to Italy, Scandinavia and eastern Europe, the expansion of its long-haul network, and the loss of up to 1,200 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Air Berlin, including its subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Belair_(airline)" title="Belair (airline)">Belair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>, planned to cut 40 of its fleet of 118 narrowbody jets, leaving Air Berlin with its own fleet of 75 aircraft. The new fleet would be 17 Airbus A330-200 for long-haul operations and 40 Airbus A320 family aircraft and 18 Bombardier Q400 aircraft for European routes.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> A separate, tourist-destination-oriented unit with 35 aircraft was to be formed, perhaps operating with a partner (<a href="/wiki/TUIfly" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly">TUIfly</a> was the assumed partner as they already operate several aircraft for Air Berlin)<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 or sold altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Plans to wet-lease the remaining aircraft were realised with the December 2016 announcement that 38 Airbus A319/A320 aircraft would be wet-leased to Lufthansa Group\'s Eurowings (33 aircraft) and Austrian Airlines (five), effective February 2017 for a period of six years.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2016, Air Berlin announced plans to close four of its seven <i>airberlin Technik</i> maintenance facilities and lay off 500 of their staff.<sup id="cite_ref-abtechnikshutdown_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abtechnikshutdown-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 December 2016, Air Berlin announced plans to sell its entire 49-percent stake in its Austrian subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a> to its own minority owner, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nikisale_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nikisale2_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale2-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> It was also announced that Niki will take over several routes to southern European, north African and Turkish leisure destinations from Air Berlin as part of the new joint-venture.<sup id="cite_ref-nikisale2_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale2-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in December 2016, Air Berlin announced the transfer of its entire fleet of 21 A321-200s to Niki and Niki\'s transfer of all its 5 A319-100s and 13 A320-200s to Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-ch051216_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch051216-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Air Berlin would discontinue its wet-lease with TUIfly.<sup id="cite_ref-ch051216_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch051216-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2017, Air Berlin announced that for summer 2017, most leisure routes were to be either transferred to <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a> or cancelled altogether and that some domestic and European city routes were to be dropped, leaving little more than the Berlin-Tegel and D\xc3\xbcsseldorf hub operations.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 April 2017, a loss of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a> \xe2\x88\x92781.9 million was announced for 2016, from a revenue of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>3.79 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_report_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_report-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in late April 2017, Air Berlin confirmed the creation of <i>Air Berlin Aeronautics <a href="/wiki/GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="GmbH">GmbH</a></i>, a new subsidiary which was to have its own operational licence (AOC) to take over the <a href="/wiki/Wetlease" class="mw-redirect" title="Wetlease">wetlease</a> operations handled by Air Berlin on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a>. Therefore, the "actual" Air Berlin will focus on operations under its own brand name.<sup id="cite_ref-abaeronautics_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abaeronautics-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2017, Air Berlin announced it would buy <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtgesellschaft_Walter" class="mw-redirect" title="Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter">Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter</a> entirely, in which it had a controlling stake since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bankruptcy">Bankruptcy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bankruptcy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After <a href="/wiki/Etihad" class="mw-redirect" title="Etihad">Etihad</a> stopped financial support, Air Berlin entered insolvency procedures on 15 August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> On 9 October 2017, Air Berlin told its staff that it would cease all remaining operations under its own <i>AB</i> flight numbers due to its negative financial outlook and bankruptcy proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-ABshutdown_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABshutdown-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 12 October 2017, Lufthansa agreed to buy 81 aircraft and employ 3,000 Air Berlin employees for \xe2\x82\xac210 million, taking over the subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtgesellschaft_Walter" class="mw-redirect" title="Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter">Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter</a> with a total of 1700 employees.\n</p><p>On 24 October 2017, the Berliner <i>Zeitfracht Group</i> confirmed it would take over the <i>Leisure Cargo</i> D\xc3\xbcsseldorf company and its 60 employees. The creditors\' committee approved a corresponding submission. Leisure Cargo conveys freight space on passenger flights.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On 27 October 2017, it was announced that a \'consortium\' of <a href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair,_and_operations" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintenance, repair, and operations">maintenance, repair, and operations</a> provider <i>Nayak Aircraft Services GmbH &amp; Co. KG</i> and Berliner <i>Zeitfracht Group</i> would purchase airberlin Technik, keeping over 300 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The final long-haul flight, from <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf</a>, was operated on 15 October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-lap_of_honour_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lap_of_honour-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> On 27 October 2017, Air Berlin\'s final flight was operated by Airbus A320 D-ABNW. It departed from Munich at 21:36 and landed at Berlin Tegel at 22:45.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 October 2017, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> would absorb 1,000 employees and lease 25 Airbus A320 aircraft for flights from Berlin Tegel for \xe2\x82\xac40 million.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span Berlin.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Air Berlin PLC shares were publicly traded on <a href="/wiki/Xetra_(trading_system)" title="Xetra (trading system)">Xetra</a> and on the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a> in the regulated market. Trading in the regulated unofficial market occurred at the exchanges in Berlin, D\xc3\xbcsseldorf, Hamburg, Munich and Stuttgart.<sup id="cite_ref-Report_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Report-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Since December 2011, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> was the largest shareholder in Air Berlin. As of December 2015, the major shareholders (over 5%) were:<sup id="cite_ref-2015_report_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_report-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" align="center" style="margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name\n</th>\n<th>Interest\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways PJSC</a></td>\n<td align="center">29.21&#160;%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>ESAS Holding AS (owners of <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a>)</td>\n<td align="center">12.02&#160;%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Other shareholders</td>\n<td align="center">58.77&#160;%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Total</b></td>\n<td align="center"><b>100.00&#160;%</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_trends">Business trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Business trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Close_up-profile_pic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Close_up-profile_pic.jpg/340px-Close_up-profile_pic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1786" data-file-height="2167" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div from 2016 to February 2017.</div></div></div>\n<p>Air Berlin was loss-making for several years. The key figures for the whole Air Berlin Group (including <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>) for the full years of operation leading up to its closure were (as at year ending 31 December):\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" href="#cite_note-2016_load_factor-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_school">Flight school</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Flight school">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Air Berlin trained its own pilots since 2007 in a joint venture with the TFC K\xc3\xa4ufer flight school. Commercial pilot training lasted around 24 months. The Air Berlin flight school was the first flight school in Germany to be awarded a training licence by the German Department of Aviation for the new Multi-Crew Pilot Licence concept in February 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_services">Technical services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Technical services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Air Berlin had its own maintenance and overhaul branch, <i>airberlin technik</i> with facilities in Berlin, D\xc3\xbcsseldorf, Munich, Stuttgart, Frankfurt, Hamburg, and Nuremberg, which employed 1300 staff as of October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-abtechnikshutdown_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abtechnikshutdown-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The technical branch was a certified EASA Part-145 maintenance organization with approximately 1200 employees providing services to both Air Berlin group aircraft and customers throughout Europe. airberlin technik was recognized and approved by various National Airworthiness Authorities such as USA FAA-145, Canadian CAA-145, Aruba EASA-145, Federal Aviation Authority of Russia, GCAA, United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In October 2016, Air Berlin announced it would close the technical bases in Stuttgart, Frankfurt, Hamburg and Nuremberg while laying off 500 staff due to restructuring measures.<sup id="cite_ref-abtechnikshutdown_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abtechnikshutdown-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Air_Berlin_destinations" title="List of Air Berlin destinations">List of Air Berlin destinations</a></div>\n<p>Prior to its shutdown, Air Berlin flew to scheduled year-round and seasonal destinations in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Walter">LGW</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Embraer_190" class="mw-redirect" title="Embraer 190">Embraer 190</a>\n</td>\n<td>3\n</td>\n<td>2013\n</td>\n<td>2013\n</td>\n<td>Transferred from <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a> and subsequently returned, were operated by <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtgesellschaft_Walter" class="mw-redirect" title="Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter">LGW</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Fokker_100" title="Fokker 100">Fokker 100</a>\n</td>\n<td>18\n</td>\n<td>2004\n</td>\n<td>2010\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_cabins">Aircraft cabins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Aircraft cabins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-111,_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-111,_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air Berlin <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319-100">Airbus A319-100</a> cabin</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-haul_flights">Long-haul flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Long-haul flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Air Berlin long-haul aircraft featured business and economy class sections. At the beginning of 2012, Air Berlin started the renewal of its long-haul cabin, equipping both economy class and business class with new seats and a new in-flight entertainment system. Fully automatic seats that could tilt up to 170 degrees were provided in business class, along with an anti-thrombosis edition and an adjustable headrest, and more legroom and a narrower seat back in economy class. All seats have an 8.9-inch monitor with a touch screen and offer movies, series, music, audiobooks and games.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In January 2013 the airline again presented a new business class which replaced the one introduced a year earlier. The new business class had single seats, offering travellers even more privacy. The new seats had a full-flat function, a massage function, and featured a 15-inch monitor.<sup id="cite_ref-business_class_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business_class-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Short-_and_medium-haul_flights">Short- and medium-haul flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Short- and medium-haul flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Business class was not offered on its short- and medium-haul flights until Air Berlin announced its introduction in August 2016. All short- and medium-haul aircraft began to feature business class in row 1 with expanded services including an empty middle seat.<sup id="cite_ref-newbusinessclass_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newbusinessclass-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_services">Passenger services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Passenger services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG/220px-Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG/330px-Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG/440px-Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air Berlin check-in counters</div></div></div>\n<p>In contrast to European pure low-cost carriers, Air Berlin offered free in-flight snacks and drinks until September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Newspapers and magazines were available on domestic German flights.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Full hot meals were complimentary on long-haul flights. On all Air Berlin routes with a flight time of 60 minutes or longer, gourmet meals were offered, which were, according to the airline, created by chefs at "Sansibar", a famous restaurant on the island of <a href="/wiki/Sylt" title="Sylt">Sylt</a>. The airline also offered in-flight entertainment, assigned seating and guaranteed flight connections.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\nAir Berlin\'s basic fares were nonrefundable and not changeable, so unused flights were a complete loss for the purchaser.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequent_flyer_program">Frequent flyer program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Frequent flyer program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Air Berlin\'s <a href="/wiki/Frequent_flyer_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Frequent flyer program">frequent flyer program</a> was called <i>topbonus</i>. Points, known as miles, could be collected on flights operated by Air Berlin, Niki, Oneworld airline partners, and selected other airlines. Accrued miles could be redeemed for award flights, or for an upgrade to business class. In addition to the entry-level "topbonus Card Classic" there were cards with Silver, Gold, and Platinum status, corresponding to Oneworld Ruby, Sapphire, and Emerald statuses. A Service Card and a Credit Card, for which a charge was made, were also available.\n</p><p>Etihad purchased a 70% stake in topbonus for \xe2\x82\xac184 million in 2012. Following the insolvency of Air Berlin, topbonus also filed for insolvency on 25 August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In over 39 years of operations, Air Berlin never suffered an accident or incident resulting in the loss of life or an aircraft.\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 18 October 2017, Air Berlin\'s last long-haul flight, Flight AB7001, <i>D-ABXA</i>, an Airbus A330-223, performed a <a href="/wiki/Go-around" title="Go-around">go-around</a> to commemorate the event and flew over the terminal, against standard <a href="/wiki/Missed_approach" title="Missed approach">go-around procedures</a>, while landing at <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport</a>. ADS-B information reports that the aircraft was at approximately 100&#160;ft or 30 m, as it passed over the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> It is reported that the crew gained permission from air traffic control prior to performing the maneuver. The passengers applauded the farewell. Both pilots were suspended pending the outcome of an investigation by <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtbundesamt" class="mw-redirect" title="Luftfahrtbundesamt">Luftfahrtbundesamt</a>, the German aviation authority.<sup id="cite_ref-lap_of_honour_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lap_of_honour-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a
